text:
The first time I made these I followed the directions exactly and they were OUTSTANDING; light and fluffy as air.  The second time I made them I did not have any buttermilk in house so I made some buttermilk using milk and vinegar.  The second batch was good but nowhere near as good, or as light and fluffy as the first batch I made with the real buttermilk.  I don't know why they weren't as fluffy but if I have any recommendations to make I would tell you to use the real buttermilk for the best results!  Added fresh blueberries to the buttermilk batter and they were delicious that way as well!  This is so very simple to mix together, that I will never use the packaged pancake mixes again.  When I double this I double all the ingredients except for the salt.  I just love making things from scratch for my family whenever I can and this is just as simple as a boxed mix, but much, much better!!!!! Update!  I added a teaspoon of Vanilla Extract to the batter - took this recipe OVER THE TOP!

text:
I tried this recipe as written and should have known better about the amount of salt it calls for.  A 1/4 Teaspn per cup of flour is enough.  I also think I would cut the baking soda next time to 1/2 teaspn per cup of flour as well.  There's sodium in baking soda.  With the recipe written as it is, I have to give it one star due to the high sodium content.  The recipe as written with the amount of salt plus baking soda makes the pancakes taste like brine.  I couldn't eat it.  I don't mean to be harsh but if anyone tries the recipe as written they will see what I mean.  Next time I will make the adjustments and think it will turn out excellent pancakes.

Yay! Homemade, easy to make pancakes and as someone else mentioned they do taste like Cracker Barrel pancakes! No more Bisquick mix for me. :) The batter was very thick for me, so I added a little more buttermilk to make it a little easier to spread, but I think its because my flour was packed down pretty hard, so there was probably more than 1 cup in there. My son loves them - he devoured three and had one without syrup just because he liked the taste so much. He's already scheming about having the 1 leftover pancake for dessert!

text:
I made these over the holidays while staying with my parents.  My mom accidently bought buttermilk instead of regular milk and wanted to get rid of it.  Boy is this the recipe to do it with.  I am a hard core breakfast eater/maker on the weekends, so I have made my fair share of pancakes over the years.  They all pale in comparison now.  If you like a light BUTTERY pancake then look no further.  They were so delicious most of us ate them plain.  The texture is unbelievably light (if you like your pancakes huge and heavy like a manhole cover this is not the recipe for you).  Now that says something.  They were also good with syrup or jam.  I was very careful not to over mix and let them sit like others recommended.  It does make a small batch - enough to feed my husband and myself and give my mom one.  These are definitely my new go to pancake recipe.  However, I think have the real buttermilk is probably essential.  Yum.  Time to go to the store!

text:
I made these again and had to change my rating because these pancakes are fab but only with syrup.  The saltiness mentioned in the negative reviews is only evident if you eat them plain or with something other than syrup.  With the syrup, however, they are fantastic tasting.  Plus, they are not as light and fluffy as you would hope.  I think I might try to add a smidge more flour next time to make them fluffier.  If you like pancakes with something other than syrup, I would recommend cutting the salt by half and adding a bit of sugar.  Here in Ireland, most people eat pancakes with their hands rolled up with butter and jam or even plain so this recipe "as is" would not be a great hit here!

text:
Cut the salt in half -- that's the ONLY change I made, based on reviews. I was hesitant to make them at all, but needed to use up buttermilk, so I tried them. Made them for my sons, so just expected to "taste" them. I ate two! They "look" heavy, but are not -- light and fluffy, in fact. USE buttermilk and do NOT over stir! Batter should be very lumpy. I cooked using NO OIL on a nonstick skillet. My nephew's a chef and says NEVER use oil for pancakes! He's right -- try it.

Great buttermilk pancake recipe.  Quick and simple, just don't over mix the batter, gently stir so the buttermilk and baking soda activate.  Buttermilk lends itself a bit "salty" so if you're sensitive to salty taste, cut back on the salt to 1/2 tsp.   Can't go wrong.

text:
I like to cook but don't feel I'm qualified to even call myself an amateur.  Notwithstanding, I've learned a few tips on how to enhance certain things.  When it comes to pancakes I like to use every little trick I can to make them turn out great because plain buttermilk pancakes are my favorite food in the whole world.  I have been trying to duplicate the flavor and texture of the ones served at the Original Pancake House and have tried adding different flavors and sourdough starters.  I fluff the egg whites, add sugar, vanilla, bring everything to room temp. etc. trying to make the perfect light golden brown buttermilk  pancake.
Today, I decided to keep my tricks to myself and just follow this recipe exactly as is was written.  The results left me humbled.  
This was by far the best buttermilk pancake recipe I have ever tried.  I have previously been a fan of Burygold's recipe on this site but this one blows that one out of the water.
I didn't do anything fancy, I just mixed the dry ingredients together (I did use Saco powdered buttermilk) then added the wet ingredients.  I mixed them together with a wooden spoon until just blended (the batter was lumpy).  I set my electric griddle to 330 degrees and very lightly greased it with canola oil.  I didn't wait until bubbles popped on the top and therefore didn't overcook them.
WOW!!!  They didn't match the unique flavor of the OPH but they were very light and fluffy and extremely delicious topped with butter and syrup.

text:
I love love love this buttermilk pancake recipe.  We've made it many times.   I dislike sugar in the batter, which is just one reason I love this recipe.  Also,  I salt every recipe to taste.  A good cook should always salt to taste and it will vary from one cook to another.  I personally like to add about 1/4 c. additional buttermilk to this recipe to stretch it.  Buttermilk does have a unique taste and perhaps some of the negative reviews are because they just don't care for buttermilk and think it's too much salt called -  i.e. the previous reviewer emphasized saltiness and bitterness.  I really don't understand the review, except they may want to stick with a fluffy pancake recipe without buttermilk.   Now this is just my opinion, but if you must add sugar and vanilla to the recipe, it becomes a new recipe. The simplicity of this particular recipe makes it a winner to me!!

text:
This is great! I omit the salt because I find baking soda to add plenty of salt for me, and I tend to add about two teaspoons of white sugar to my batter to get these to brown up beautifully. Just my preference! Also, these work really well subbing out buttermilk (vingar + milk, lemon juice + milk, plain yogurt thinned with milk or water, etc) if you don't happen to have any buttermilk on hand. I still recommend trying the buttermilk in this recipe though; it's unbeatable! Great recipe.
(TIP: melt your butter in your preheating pancake pan; any butter residue leftover just saves you the step of greasing the pan! Also, don't re-grease after the first pancake. The butter in the batter will keep it from sticking, and if you add a bit of sugar these will come out pretty and golden like restaurant style flapjacks!)

userID:

Display Name:
MeOhmy
isPro:

https://images.media-allrecipes.com/userphotos/50x50/5674133.jpg
city:
None
region:
None
country:
None
text:
I have tried many pancake recipes, but this one takes the cake lol! I used buttermilk powder instead of fresh buttermilk for mine and they turned out amazing. It gives just the right amount of tangy and creamy flavor. You can find buttermilk powder next to the baking supplies (flour sugar etc.) in the grocery store. Basically you just mix it with water and viola buttermilk. So I pretty much followed the recipe except for subbing the powdered buttermilk about 5 tbsp and about 1 1/4 c  to 1 3/4 c of water (depending on how thick you like the batter). I also added a few tbsp sugar and 1 tbsp vanilla extract. I just mix all of the dry ingredients together like the recipe says and then mix my buttermilk powder in with the dry stuff. Then add the eggs and melted butter (careful not to add hot butter we don't want scrambled eggs). Last add the water, watching the consistency of the batter as you pour it in and whisk so it doesn't get too thin (don't over mix). Remember after you open the buttermilk powder to store in the fridge. So simple and sooo delicious! Easy ingredients to have on hand. My family loves this recipe! 
Note: Trial and error has shown me to use less liquid in the recipe when you are subbing the powdered buttermilk for fresh. Fresh is pretty thick so you need more. Also you may have to play w the amount of buttermilk powder you add according to the amount of tangy flavor you personally like, 5or 6 tbsp. was good for us.

city:

region:
None
country:
None
text:
This would be a 2-star if they hadn't turned out so fluffy. Many reviewers said this was too salty but many also said this was perfect as-is, so I thought I'd give the author the benefit of the doubt and try it as-is. The batter was wonderfully fluffy, and the pancakes rose beautifully while cooking. Though the fluffiness is perfect, the flavor was VERY salty and bitter from the baking soda. I tried again and cut the salt in half, added 3 tsp sugar and a few drops vanilla and the flavor was a little more balanced, and still just as fluffy, but they were still salty and my husband did not like them, even with syrup. This batter is very thick and takes a bit longer to cook, so I found turning the heat down to medium and keeping a close eye on them kept them from getting too brown. IF I make this again, I will reduce the salt to 1/4 tsp, add 3 tsp sugar and 2 drops vanilla. Also, I added about 2 or 3 tsp more buttermilk the second time and it was not necessary to spread the batter with the cup, they turned out perfectly round and still just as fluffy.

text:
Alright, I'm no master baker but pancakes should be pretty easy, right??? Wrong!!!!!! This recipe leaves out a few important tips that you need to know. 

First of all, DO NOT FORGET to sift your dry ingredients together before adding the wet ingredients!!!!! If you don't sift the dry ingredients, you will be hit with a salt pocket in the middle of your pancake. My second complaint is that these aren't sweet enough, although that's a personal opinion. Next time I will be adding some sugar on top of vanilla extract. 

They did turn out as fluffy as advertised! Just be warned, the directions are not complete.

city:
None
region:
None
country:
None
text:
I searched many buttermilk pancake recipes after seeing my guy seriously impressed by some uberperfect ones he ordered in one of my favorite breakfast spots. I decided to give a try to making them from scratch. I usually don't make them, or if I have to, it's from a package mix.   This recipe seemed the easiest and made sense, so I followed it almost exactly with a few exceptions:   1: I added 1+ teaspoon vanilla with the wet ingredients. (There were just a few drops beyond 1 teaspoon left in the bottle, so I emptied it!) 2: I only used 1/4 teaspoon salt, after reading the reviews. This was adequate. I wouldn't add more than that when I make them again.  3: I added 1 tablespoon sugar to the dry ingredients. 4: He liked how puffy the ones he ordered were, so I separated the egg, whipped the white till very foamy, almost stiff, and folded it in at the very end. I do think this helped make them more light and fluffy.   I think this was a great recipe, and I think it will be the one I use when I make them again. I think the flavor was great and the texture of the ones that turned out right was very nice. I really don't make pancakes often, so I will need to perfect the process of cooking them correctly.   I used butter to cook them in and I think it burns too fast. I would either use cooking spray (blech) or canola oil.  Also, I'd like to eventually incorporate whole wheat flour to make it a healthier breakfast.

Didn't have fresh buttermilk on hand, so I reconstituted some SaCo powdered buttermilk (only substitution). Of course, she still ate 3 saucer-sized pancakes with gusto. :)  I plan to order more powdered buttermilk and make this recipe next weekend.

text:
These are UNBELIEVABLE!!!  I've made them 4 times, already and my hubby and kids LOVE them.  
I made the recipe as written (I thought) the first time, but it turns out I had too much flour.  Even so, I added more and more buttermilk until they were JUST pourable.  They turned out fabulous!  The 2nd time I made them was weird.  I'm not sure what happened-I made them exactly as written and though the flavor was good, the texture was not.  It was bumpy and squishy in places.  The pancakes themselves came out flat and flabby.  I'm not sure exactly what went wrong, but I suspect the buttermilk I used wasn't good.  I'm pretty sure it had nothing to do with the recipe, because the 3rd and 4th time I made these were a hit.  They turned out PERFECTLY.  The 4th time I made them, I added about 1/2 TBS of cinnamon and 3 capfuls of vanilla, by the way.  STUPID DELICIOUS.  :)
The recipe does a great job of describing the way the batter (almost dough) should look, and that is REALLY helpful (especially for those of us used to making instant just-add-water pancakes).  
I will never, EVER make instant pancakes again!!  Thank you SOOOOO much for freeing me and my family!  :)

text:
These are pancake perfection! I have been looking for a recipe for made-from-scratch pancakes, and now my Bisquick days are over. I took the advice of the reviewer who said to reduce the salt in the recipe, so I used 1/2 a teaspoon of salt instead of a whole teaspoon. I was able to make 8 medium-width, thick pancakes from this. They had a buttery flavor, and a soft and fluffy texture.  They didn't absorb too much syrup, either. I was also able to eat one plain, without butter on top, since there is such a butter-y taste within the pancakes.

This was our Christmas morning breakfast today, and it was perfect! Cinnken, thanks for sharing.

I read the ingredients on what I thought was a healthier boxed version for pancakes, saw it had "bleached" flour and threw the box in the trash!  We don't have pancakes very often, but I knew I had to find a healthy, delicious and easy recipe! This is a good one. I made the batter yesterday, had the pancakes this morning with unsalted butter and real maple syrup!! Keeper!  Tweak it yourself if you like, have fun with a basic good recipe.  I will add melted coconut oil along with the butter next time, maybe mix 1/4 c each of coconut flour and whole wheat flour to the basic recipe!  I'll let u know how it turns out!

text:
This one deserves more stars on the simplicity and finished product! I was looking for a quick buttermilk recipe that required a few ingredients, and not a huge list.  I used low fat buttermilk, whole white wheat flour and 1 tsp. vanilla and left out the butter.  They came out fluffy and delicious! It was like we went to the popular pancake house, but these were tastier and HEALTHIER! You can't tell that these are whole wheat with the using white wheat.---------------------UPDATE:  These are just so good and easy to whip up.  I made them again with whole white wheat and added frozen blueberries.  I leave out the butter in the batter and just use it to top my pancakes, if I want.  Just so yummy!  Don't forget to add 1 tsp of vanilla!  I never get 12 pancakes from this recipe, more like 6.  If cooking for more than 3 people, you will have to double or triple the recipe.

text:
I made this recipe just as stated.  They were so light and fluffy. No more box mixes for me! As others have said, they were salty,  but I contribute that to my error and not necessarily the recipe's fault.  I used melted margarine instead of butter.  There is a considerable difference in sodium between the two...margarine 1Tbsp 130mg-butter 1Tbsp 3mg.  I also noticed there is a considerable amount in the buttermilk I use.  Next time will cut the salt at least in half and use butter instead.  Lesson for me is ...don't fault a recipe if I don't read all the labels for my ingredients.
Made it again this morning.   1/4 tsp salt and 1/4tsp baking soda.  Perfect!

text:
I made these pancakes today using the ingredients as listed. The only thing I did differently was that I mixed the dry ingredients together in one bowl, and mixed the wet ingredients together in another bowl. I also let the wet ingredients come to room temperature before gently folding the wet into the dry. I would think it would be difficult to not overmix if you added one wet ingredient after another into the dry. These cooked up very fluffy and made 8 large pancakes. We did notice the salt, but it wasn't overwhelming. I will cut the salt in half next time, but these were easy to make and tasted delicious. 4 stars for unclear directions.

Both versions were light, fluffy, tender and very easy to make.  Love buttermilk!

Easy and Delicious! When I read the recipe, 1 tsp salt sounded a little too much salt to me, so I went with my gut feeling and only added 1/2 tsp salt. I think it was perfect that way, I didn't want it to be any saltier. Second time I tried it, I added 1 tbsp sugar and 1/2 tsp salt. This version came out great too. Both times I used real buttermilk. If you have any doubts about adding a whole teaspoon of salt, my suggestion is to try making it with 1/2 tsp salt first, and then see if you want it any saltier. This is going to be my go-to recipe for pancakes from now on!

text:
Excellent pancakes! Make your own buttermilk by adding lemon juice or white vinegar to regular milk (I used a tablespoon of each). Stir it in and leave it for a few minutes before adding to the rest of the pancake mixture. If you have leftover Ricotta cheese, I highly recommend adding 1/4 to 1/3 cup to the batter for really splendid pancakes. I added a couple more tablespoons of flour to compensate for the additional volume from the added Ricotta cheese. Topped off with hot syrup and sliced fresh strawberries -with whipped cream, if you like - my family loved them.

text:
This is a great and simply recipe.  It taste great much like old fashion buttermilk pancakes.  I gave it 3 stars because of the amount of salt.  I was concerned about using 1 teaspoon in a recipe that only has 12 servings.  However I followed the recipe exactly as it is written.  You can taste salt and if you view the nutrietion information you will see that the sodium milligrams far exceed the allowable amount per daily serving.  I will make this recipe again but I will reduce the amount of salt.  If you like salt and don't have any health issues related to high sodium content then this may be okay for you.  However,  if you need to watch your sodium please reduce it for this recipe.

text:
I'm not a pancake person.  I know, shocking.  I am the only one I've ever met.  I don't like maple syrup, and I don't like pancakes soggy with maple syrup.  Whenever I try to make pancakes I waste half the batter trying to get the heat and timing right.  Also pancakes, to me, always have a weird, slightly metallic taste, like there's too much baking powder or something.  However, I don't think I've ever had homemade pancakes before.  I was browsing on here late at night and these sounded really good, so I whipped them up.  I used a vinegar and water substitute for the buttermilk.  I'll have to try them another time with real buttermilk, but even as they were I really liked them.  I had them with peanut butter.  I didn't notice any of the weird taste I usually get with pancakes.  I'm guessing that taste probably comes from some unnecessary additive in the mix.  My only other complaint was that these seemed a little salty.  I might use unsalted butter next time or go with half a teaspoon of salt.  With how easy and cheap these were to make from scratch, I don't know why anyone ever uses a mix.  Next time I want to add the vanilla, as someone suggested in the comments.  I burned just as many as usual, but these were good enough I might take the time to become a pancake person!

I had mine with homemade strawberry syrup, my daughter had homemade cherry syrup, and my son went for chocolate chips - all three were excellent. I also like the amount it makes, the last pancake recipe I tried here made about 5 times more than we needed and even though it said it refrigerated well, it didn't - this was the perfect amount and I would rather make a new batch each time than use leftover batter.  I like that with no added sugar or flavorings, they were such a great vehicle for toppings.  thank you for the great recipe!

text:
I've been looking for a good buttermilk pancake recipe for a while, and this is it! I did make a couple changes to the recipe. I used only 1/2 teaspoon salt, and I added 1/8 cup of sugar. I also normally double the recipe, and it produces 10-12 pancakes. The whole family (including my mom and dad, who were visiting the first time I tried it) loved them. They have just the right flavor.

I'm glad the recipe mentioned that the batter is thick. It's definitely less runny than any other pancake recipe I've tried. Make sure you spread it out with the measuring cup on the griddle so they don't come out too thick. Also, the uncooked side may not bubble as much as other recipes, so make sure you don't overcook them. 2-3 minutes per side at 300 F seems to work well.

Made these this morning to celebrate a snow day off from school (I have a 10 year old). I always scan the reviews before I make something, and in this case, I saw the recommendation for less salt. I put 1/2 tsp instead of a whole teaspoon. I also used unsalted butter.  They were great! I did taste a little of the batter, and even with the 1/2 tsp, it tasted a smidge salty. But the finished product was yummy!  I served with some warm real maple syrup.

I also didn't have fresh buttermilk, so I used buttermilk powder. It's great stuff, buttermilk powder. You just add it to the dry ingredients, then use water in place of the buttermilk, and it works great for anything calling for buttermilk. 

The recipe made six large pancakes, so I'll have some to freeze. My son wouldn't taste them, since he's really not a breakfast person. More for me!

But what I did, I made the batter up at 2am and put it in the frig until not long ago (at about 11:45am). I split up the batter and made some plain and some banana walnut pancakes. I added 1/2 banana mashed, about 9 whole walnut pieces chopped up fine, and a 1/2 teaspoon of Ceylon cinnamon. It was really good! I used all the batter and made everything now so tomorrow I can just heat and eat. I made great BIG plate size pancakes just like IHOP. I'm sitting here stuffed now and don't want to move! But I know the dishes have to be done unfortunately. I wish my fairy godmother would do them for me.

First batch I made as written and didn't bother my children one bit but I as an adult had to step back and realize I did not like the flavor, hence a 4 star rating.  With that being said, I went for this modified version and was extremely pleased, but be warned it most likely will still be too salty for some.  My version I would rate 5 stars.  1/2 tsp salt, 3/4 tsp Baking soda, 1/2 tsp sugar, and definitely salted butter. Spoon flour into your 1 cup measure.. NEVER PACK IT IN!! I hope this helps some folks and doesn't get lost among all the reviews.

No one in my family liked these pancakes, even after drowning them in syrup.  We did not like the flavor, which I suspect is due to the relatively high amount of salt and the lack of sugar to balance out the buttermilk.

On a positive note, the texture was fluffy.

I'm not sure if it's something I am doing wrong or my old vintage "griddle in the middle" 1955. I make French toast, pancakes, and anything else that is made on a griddle and it all comes out fine. I just cannot figure out what went wrong with these pancakes!!  My non picky eaters (but know excellent food) were not impressed with these pancakes at all. text:
This recipe has way too much baking soda.  When you take a bite, the flavor is good, but the aftertaste is nothing but the soda flavor.  While the batter itself was VERY salty, I did not taste too much salt in the cooked pancakes.  My daughter LOVES pancakes, but would not eat these after the first bite.  I will try this recipe again, cutting the salt and soda in half, and perhaps adding a little vanilla.

text:
I guess this is proof that just because a recipe gets good reviews, that doesn't mean it will be good for me! After reading the reviews, I figured that a couple of minor changes they suggested would be ok. We had no buttermilk, so I did the 1 cup milk to 1 T vinegar, which seemed to work well. I also added a little bit of sugar. For some reason my batter was very thin and the more I stirred, the thinner it seemed to get. Also the places where there were still lumps were VERY salty! Enough syrup can disguise that probably, but I tend to go light on it. Not sure what exactly went so wrong, but these didn't work well for us :(
